  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_edc2cde2-d7e9-4847-bd55-1634fec585b6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

All she knows when she comes to in a ransacked cabin is that there are two men arguing over whether or not to kill her.<br/><br/>And that she must run.<br/><br/>In her riveting style, April Henry crafts a nail-biting thriller involving murder, identity theft, and biological warfare. Follow Cady and Ty (her accidental savior turned companion), as they race against the clock to stay alive.<br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13404655459245382976">This was a super quick read that I started while waiting to find out what my next challenge would be. I wasn't expecting much and was, therefore, pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471800814ra/20108805.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Unlike all the problems I had with The Progeny, where the premise was faulty at best, Cady's story was totally believable. While she, too, had lost her memory, it was due to trauma, and this in no way prevented her from making reasonable, logic-based decisions.<br/><br/>The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die checks all the [read my] boxes:<br/>+Intelli</span>
  <span id="freeText13404655459245382976" style="display:none">This was a super quick read that I started while waiting to find out what my next challenge would be. I wasn't expecting much and was, therefore, pleasantly surprised.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471800814ra/20108805.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unlike all the problems I had with The Progeny, where the premise was faulty at best, Cady's story was totally believable. While she, too, had lost her memory, it was due to trauma, and this in no way prevented her from making reasonable, logic-based decisions.<br><br>The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die checks all the [read my] boxes:<br>+Intelligent, self-sufficient protagonist - check<br>+Sweet boy - check<br>+Character development - check<br>+Believable plot - check<br>+Fast-paced - check<br>+Happy ending - check</span>

<div id="review_563171895" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/563171895" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/563171895?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs-netgalley">arcs-netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563171895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17670104847209698929">A copy of The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die was provided to me by Henry Holt and Co. (BYR)/Netgalley for review purposes.<br/><br/><i>'[...]my mind shut down. Went blank. Went someplace where I wouldn't have to remember.'</i><br/><br/>What would you do if you woke up to find you had been kidnapped? What would you do if you somehow manage to escape but realize you have no idea where you were? What would you do if you didn't have any idea who you were? The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die is a riveting thriller of a girl who has</span>
  <span id="freeText17670104847209698929" style="display:none">A copy of The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die was provided to me by Henry Holt and Co. (BYR)/Netgalley for review purposes.<br><br><i>'[...]my mind shut down. Went blank. Went someplace where I wouldn't have to remember.'</i><br><br>What would you do if you woke up to find you had been kidnapped? What would you do if you somehow manage to escape but realize you have no idea where you were? What would you do if you didn't have any idea who you were? The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die is a riveting thriller of a girl who has to piece together the past so she can live to see the future. <br><br>I've read April Henry's 'The Night She Disappeared' and it's an incredibly short yet fast-paced mystery which I really enjoyed. To me, 'The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die' is also short and fast-paced yet more complex and required more pages in order to properly flush out the mystery. The pieces of the puzzle don't start coming together until near the very end and once the pieces started forming they left me with an unnaturally rushed feeling that I felt could have been avoided with more explanation/pages. <br><br>There were a few issues I had in particular: <br>The 'bad guys' were inherently bad and lacked any sort of complexity thus making them quite a bore. Plus, it always makes me giggle when the bad guys completely reveal all their plans right before they intent on killing you. <br>Also, there was a strange and unnecessary reference to a gay character. <br><i>'His voice swoops up and down. He sounds more gay than before. I wonder if he's doing it deliberately - to make them think there would be no reason for him to give a girl shelter.'</i><br>Which... makes zero sense. Because he's a gay man he couldn't possibly have any 'girl' friends? Or even possible care about their well-being? That passage just struck me as completely irrelevant.<br>Also, there wasn't a love-interest exactly but there was a male character that became involved in her <s>drama</s> trouble. After meeting him while trying to hide from the 'bad guys' he realizes she's in dire need of help and assists in getting her past them. In my opinion, that should have been the end of their relationship but instead this guy basically risks the possible destruction of any future he may have for this girl he doesn't know. It just wasn't plausible. There was a slight explanation given for his 'need' to help her and it kind of make sense but still didn't completely work for me in way of explanation.<br><br>Despite my issues, I did still mostly enjoy The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die. It is fast-paced, exciting, and definitely suspenseful. <br><br>*All quotes taken are from an uncorrected proof*<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://sweet-tidbits.blogspot.com/" title="Sweet Tidbits" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351064i/704765.gif" alt="Sweet Tidbits" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="17670104847209698929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

After that there are some bumps and near-misses, and the plot speeds past the warning lights. <br/>April Henry spins a fun—but messy— ride that leads ultimately nowhere, but was worth the thrill. <br/>I would’ve liked if the book had been a little longer and not as rushed, especially toward the end, to give us time to fully grasp the weight of the mystery and let the suspense simmer. <br/>Not her best, but definitely not the worst. <br/></span>

<div id="review_1742294147" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1742294147" />
    <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books"><img alt="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527965221p2/19967008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742294147?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)" href="/user/show/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books">Danielle (The Blonde Likes Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=btb-challenge-2017">btb-challenge-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19967008-danielle-the-blonde-likes-books?shelf=thrillers-mystery">thrillers-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742294147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9585903010390801088">After waking up in a cabin with no memory of how she got there, Cady starts to panic. Soon after regaining consciousness, she hears her captors talking hears one of them tell the other to take her out back and “finish her off”. After managing to escape, she has no idea where to go…she has no money, doesn’t remember her name, and doesn’t know what happened to her.<br/><br/>In her run from these men, she meets Ty, who ends up accompanying her on her journey to get to safety. What Cady does know is that she’</span>
  <span id="freeText9585903010390801088" style="display:none">After waking up in a cabin with no memory of how she got there, Cady starts to panic. Soon after regaining consciousness, she hears her captors talking hears one of them tell the other to take her out back and “finish her off”. After managing to escape, she has no idea where to go…she has no money, doesn’t remember her name, and doesn’t know what happened to her.<br /><br />In her run from these men, she meets Ty, who ends up accompanying her on her journey to get to safety. What Cady does know is that she’s still in danger, she just doesn’t know why.<br /><br />I’ve had a few less than stellar reads lately, and I was hoping this quick thriller would be just the thing to break my drought. Unfortunately, it didn’t do it for me. It wasn’t quite what I was expecting, and felt more like an action book than a thriller. The end also took a turn I wasn’t expecting – very similar to The Outliers, which was another book I didn’t like.<br />What I did like was Cady and her friendship with Ty. I did find it a little unrealistic that they bonded so quickly and that Ty innately trusted Cady when she didn’t even know who she was or what happened to her, but they were good together and relied on each other, which while not always believable, was a nice add to the story, especially considering most of the characters weren’t super developed and were often flat.<br /><br />Overall, I don’t have a ton to say about the book, which is probably fitting considering it was only ~200 pages long. It was a very quick read, and if you like action books/movies with a touch of biological warfare, this will be the perfect choice for you. Unfortunately, I was looking for something that was more of a thriller, and this wasn’t a winner for me.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_531275256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531275256" />
    <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions"><img alt="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464118116p2/2602702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531275256?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (A Reader of Fictions)" href="/user/show/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions">Christina (A Reader of Fictions)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2602702-christina-a-reader-of-fictions?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531275256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4037732398627513123">This review is going to be uncharacteristically short for me, but the book itself is pretty short, so I suppose that's fitting. Since this is going to be one of those reviews that sort of reads like I didn't like the book, let me say this up front: I did like The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die. However, I'm giving it two stars here on GR, because overall I feel like it was an okay book, not an especially good one. I'm not generally a big fan of thrillers, but I previously quite enjoyed Henry's Gir</span>
  <span id="freeText4037732398627513123" style="display:none">This review is going to be uncharacteristically short for me, but the book itself is pretty short, so I suppose that's fitting. Since this is going to be one of those reviews that sort of reads like I didn't like the book, let me say this up front: I did like The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die. However, I'm giving it two stars here on GR, because overall I feel like it was an okay book, not an especially good one. I'm not generally a big fan of thrillers, but I previously quite enjoyed Henry's Girl, Stolen, so I hoped that I would like this one just as much. Still, TGWWSTD was a fun, quick read overall.<br /><br />In general, I would say that April Henry accomplishes what she set out to do in this book. TGWWSTD entertains. The plot moves along at a fast pace, and it's certainly never boring. The reader can't help but be curious and the pages flip by quickly. TGWWWSTD serves as the literary equivalent of a fairly mindless action movie, which isn't necessarily a bad thing.<br /><br />The techniques Henry uses to accomplish this are quite standard thriller fare, which is why my enjoyment of this one boils down purely to the sheer entertainment factor. The main character has amnesia for much of the book, waking up in a cabin as two men prepare to kill her. Sure, amnesia happens, but it's over-employed in such action plots to up the danger level, since the MC doesn't have any idea where to go or who to trust.<br /><br />Henry's writing consists of simple sentences and fragments. This style does create a sense of rushing headlong through the story. Thriller authors employ this method to create a feeling of urgency. While I do think it does work, I just generally prefer complex, more ornate writing. The combination of the writing, short chapters, and fast pace will likely make this an excellent choice for reluctant readers.<br /><br />Most every chapter ends on a mini-cliffhanger, immediately resolved on the next page. Yet again, this technique does keep the reader moving through the novel at a fast clip. It's designed to make TGWWSTD a one sitting read, because you have to keep going to answer the lingering question from the last chapter. Effective, but trite.<br /><br />While not thoroughly fleshed out, Henry's characters are sufficiently realistic for her purposes. Cady and Ty are likable enough that the reader does want them to win out over the bad guys. The skills that Cady possesses seem a bit convenient, though some are explained, like her ability to fight. What really feels unlikely is that Cady met Ty, a boy just this side of destitution, who is willing to miss class, endangering his dream of being an EMT, and work, risking putting him on the streets, to help save her from men with guns. Sure, he's nice, but, really, who's going to do that? I can see helping her when they first meet, but he's with her to the end, and I just don't see that. He also just happens to have the right amount of cash saved up so they can do what they need to do.<br /><br />The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die runs just 213 pages. With short chapters and a fast pace, it's an excellent choice when you want something you can read quickly for sheer entertainment value. Ultimately, though, it's not particularly memorable and I won't be revisiting it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4037732398627513123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3009826647" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3009826647" />
    <a title="Joey T" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/91584408-joey-t"><img alt="Joey T" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601340734p2/91584408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3009826647?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joey T" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joey T" href="/user/show/91584408-joey-t">Joey T</a>

<div id="review_579961131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579961131" />
    <a title="Jenni Arndt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6971133-jenni-arndt"><img alt="Jenni Arndt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364785651p2/6971133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579961131?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenni Arndt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenni Arndt" href="/user/show/6971133-jenni-arndt">Jenni Arndt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6971133-jenni-arndt?shelf=arc-own">arc-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579961131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14310104712771891533">Wow what a short, intense read this was. I wasn’t too sure going into it how I would fare with it because it was such a short novel and the first I have read from Henry, but I’m happy I gave this one a try. This one does not let up from page one and I was on the edge of my seat as Katie ran her butt off and tried her best to find out who she was and who was after her.<br/><br/>We catch up with Cady right in the thick of things. She wakes up beaten and bruised on the floor of a cabin and has absolutely no </span>
  <span id="freeText14310104712771891533" style="display:none">Wow what a short, intense read this was. I wasn’t too sure going into it how I would fare with it because it was such a short novel and the first I have read from Henry, but I’m happy I gave this one a try. This one does not let up from page one and I was on the edge of my seat as Katie ran her butt off and tried her best to find out who she was and who was after her.<br /><br />We catch up with Cady right in the thick of things. She wakes up beaten and bruised on the floor of a cabin and has absolutely no recollection of who she was and how she got there. She also has no idea who the two men are standing above her saying to kill her because she knows nothing. Straight away my interest was piqued, I wanted to know who these men were and why they had tortured Cady for information. What worked very well for this one was how linear the plot was. There wasn’t much romance or friendship drama to bog it down though she does make one connection along the way. When she meets Ty I liked him immediately. You could tell that he had such a kind nature but it quickly comes to light that he hasn’t had the easiest life. While that was all fine and good I did find that the extent to which he was willing to put his life on the line was a little unbelievable. I get that he likes to help out his fellow man and pay it forward but he got himself into some serious legal issues for a girl that he just randomly met at McDonalds.<br /><br />With very short chapters our attention never has the chance to stray with this one. Something is constantly happening and the tension is top notch. We don’t get a lot of layers to our bad guys as everything is revealed which is something that I would have liked a bit more of. I always appreciate when I get to see multiple sides of the bad guy and maybe even come to understand their motive. Here we get very little information about them and a head honcho who is incredibly typical. I think for what this story was, it worked. It kept the novel short and if you sit back and take it at face value too many details may have began to bog the story down a bit.<br /><br />There isn’t too much to say about this one because of how short and linear the plot is but I can say this: The Girl Who Was Supposed To Die turned out to be a great, fun way to spend a few hours on a rainy Sunday morning. If you’re looking for a quick mystery to get you out of a paranormal rut then this one could be for you.<br /><br /><i>An Advanced Reader's Copy was provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />--<br /><br /><b>You can read all of my reviews at <a href="http://www.alluringreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Alluring Reads</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14310104712771891533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1957736815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1957736815" />
    <a title="Jamilah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55288713-jamilah"><img alt="Jamilah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579605972p2/55288713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1957736815?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamilah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamilah" href="/user/show/55288713-jamilah">Jamilah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55288713-jamilah?shelf=eureka">eureka</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55288713-jamilah?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55288713-jamilah?shelf=midas_touch">midas_touch</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1957736815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7806562794657212457"> In April Henry’s stand alone novel, ‘The girl who was supposed to die’, the readers are introduced to the narrator Cadence Scott (Cady). At the beginning of the novel Cady is woken up by loud voices and finds herself in an abandoned, ransacked cabin. The voices she hears are of two men arguing about whether or not they should kill her. However, Cady does not recall how she found herself in this predicament. She does not have any memories of her past including her own name. Having woken up with </span>
  <span id="freeText7806562794657212457" style="display:none"> In April Henry’s stand alone novel, ‘The girl who was supposed to die’, the readers are introduced to the narrator Cadence Scott (Cady). At the beginning of the novel Cady is woken up by loud voices and finds herself in an abandoned, ransacked cabin. The voices she hears are of two men arguing about whether or not they should kill her. However, Cady does not recall how she found herself in this predicament. She does not have any memories of her past including her own name. Having woken up with no recollection of the past and by men discussing her death, it is Cady’s first instinct to run.<br />The novel is set within the time period of two days, with Cadence running from the men she claims are still after her. Cady meets friends along the way, who help her discover her identity. It’s a cat and mice chase, as the people out hunting will stop at nothing; only, the police claim she is a runaway mentally ill patient. Cady does not know what to believe, she feels that she can’t trust anyone, including herself. She can’t decipher a truth from a lie, and questions herself if she is an ill patient, and if that could be the cause of her sudden memory loss. As the story unfolds, Cady unravels her past and every question is answered.<br /><br /> <br />The girl who was supposed to die, is an original novel that is captivating through to the last page. It is a fast-paced, gripping novel that I read in one sitting. It surprised me to find that I immensely enjoyed reading this, as I do not usually appreciate genres of the like. Due to my low-expectations, my scoring was raised higher, as I did not believe a book could portray a traumatising event so well. Though like all books, as a reader, I found some scenes unnecessary. Some parts were unrealistic and there seemed to be a very unlikely chance of this happening. Though, I believe the plot and characters were planned well, and this caused me to have a similarity relationship with the protagonist. I felt the same way as Cady, and were banging my fists in protest in appropriate scenes, yelling at the book. By reading this novel, it has made me more conscious of what happens in today's society. In my opinion this book deserves a five out of five, and should be a must-read for everyone. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7806562794657212457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abida&#39;s Book Adventures" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abida&#39;s Book Adventures" href="/user/show/23325202-abida-s-book-adventures">Abida&#39;s Book Adventures</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer705732431" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3709488237984543256"><p>This book got your attention from the moment you started it. It was very fast and full of action. There really wasn't a dull moment in this book.</p><br/><p>Katie is an average girl who doesn't know who she is or where she is. All she knows, is that two guys are discussing on killing her and getting rid of her body and that she has to find a way to get out. She always had a plan or idea in her head through out the whole book. Ty is a normal guy working in his shift and finds a girl being chased and helps he</p></span>
  <span id="freeText3709488237984543256" style="display:none"><p>This book got your attention from the moment you started it. It was very fast and full of action. There really wasn't a dull moment in this book.</p><br /><p>Katie is an average girl who doesn't know who she is or where she is. All she knows, is that two guys are discussing on killing her and getting rid of her body and that she has to find a way to get out. She always had a plan or idea in her head through out the whole book. Ty is a normal guy working in his shift and finds a girl being chased and helps her out (from the kindness out his heart). He helps and stays by Katie the whole time (even though it's dangerous).</p> <br /><p>The book didn't have romance in it (like who has the time to fall in love with someone while being hunted down by men). But we do get know what happens between Katie and Ty. The only thing that bugged me a little was how the book was divide. Other than it was a good book.</p> </span>

<div id="review_1014324016" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1014324016" />
    <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona"><img alt="Michelle Wrona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576510116p2/15162465.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1014324016?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Wrona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Wrona" href="/user/show/15162465-michelle-wrona">Michelle Wrona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=awesome-ending">awesome-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=yum">yum</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=mystery-thriller-murder">mystery-thriller-murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=book-by-author-i-read">book-by-author-i-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=gorgeous-male-character">gorgeous-male-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=kick-ass-protagonist">kick-ass-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=expected-better">expected-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15162465-michelle-wrona?shelf=to-buy-asap">to-buy-asap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1014324016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1645162759679457860"><b> *3.5 star rating* </b><br/><br/><i>"Maybe it's because I'm average." I sniff back my tears. "Maybe it's because I'm like everyone else." Ty rolls his eyes. "I may not know you very well, but I'll tell you one thing: You aren't like anyone else."</i><br/><br/><b> Girl, Stolen was an amazing book. I couldn't wait for more from this daring, new author that's sure to leave thousands of other readers stunned with her plot-twisting mysteries. <i>The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die</i></b> wasn't as good as April Henry's other book, but it was some</span>
  <span id="freeText1645162759679457860" style="display:none"><b> *3.5 star rating* </b><br><br><i>"Maybe it's because I'm average." I sniff back my tears. "Maybe it's because I'm like everyone else." Ty rolls his eyes. "I may not know you very well, but I'll tell you one thing: You aren't like anyone else."</i><br><br><b> Girl, Stolen was an amazing book. I couldn't wait for more from this daring, new author that's sure to leave thousands of other readers stunned with her plot-twisting mysteries. <i>The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die</i></b> wasn't as good as April Henry's other book, but it was something that left me thinking.<br><br> Imagine--you wake up in some cabin that you've never seen more. You don't remember your name or even have a clue who you are, and all you hear two men talking about how you don't know anything and how they're going to go and "finish you off." What would you do? <b>This is what Cady went through.</b><br> <br> Of course, this girl escapes. I'm not going to go into full detail on how she did it, but she did. She was supposed to die, but she made it out. People are saying that she "escaped from a mental hospital," which would've been super-cheesy, but she actually didn't. This book will keep you guessing until the very end and will get you thinking about these types of situations that occur all over the world.<br><br> I'm always interested in these types of mysteries where the book is taken place from the victim's POV. I don't like the detective-police sort of stories, but this is definitely awesome for my liking. <b>I really loved the idea of a supposed-murder.</b><br><br> <b>The first page of this book captivated me.</b> I just couldn't believe that the author thought of something so unthinkable and so unbelievable. You just don't want to imagine any of these things happening, but April Henry needs us to. It's her job, haha. If you liked to get a little creeped out, then this book's perfect for you. <i>You may or may not need an escort with you at all times and will need to make sure that your parents don't own an animal-disease lab.</i> Other than that, you're all good.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407036913ra/10631524.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> And you may or may not have trouble breathing or claustrophobia because the amount of fresh air is fading away. :D<br><br> As I went on with the book, it was pretty good. By the end, I found it to be nothing special. The idea was petrifying, but something was missing and that slanted the whole book another way in another direction. Maybe this is because it's very similar to April Henry's <i>Girl, Stolen.</i> I just can't seem to figure out a reason why I'm feeling like this after reading it. By the end, I was still deciding what rating to give this book. A 3 was my first choice, but then I began counting the pros and cons, and well, let's just say the positives took over.<br><br> <b> Cady was a very believable character.</b> April Henry really made her voice stand out, and she was fairly realistic and understanding. You will feel sympathy for her 24/7 because of her situation, but because of her badass-ness, that sympathy kind of goes away a little.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407036913ra/10631525.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I loved Ty, seriously. It was kind of unbelievable how he took Cady into his home and treated her like a princess even though he heard all of those bad things about her and how she's kind of a criminal, but those things aside, <b> I loved him. </b> <br><br> The ending of this book was predictable, but I guess we all saw it coming from the start. This is a touching story that will get you fawning for more! I can't wait to read <i>The Body in the Woods!</i> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1645162759679457860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1926082502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926082502" />
    <a title="Wren " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11442507-wren"><img alt="Wren " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443235719p2/11442507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926082502?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren " href="/user/show/11442507-wren">Wren </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=exciting">exciting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=young-adult-general">young-adult-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=contemporary-young-adult">contemporary-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11442507-wren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926082502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3250415897102429626">This review can also be found at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2017/04/the-girl-who-was-supposed-to-die-by.html'>http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br/><br/> She wakes up to two men arguing over whether or not to end her life. She doesn't know her name, she doesn't know where she is, and she doesn't know why one of her fingernails has been pried off of her hand. <br/><br/>She manages to escape, but her ordeal is far from over. As she investigates herself, who she is, and what is going on, she gets help from an acquaintance who is determined to solve this mystery with her. Only one thing </span>
  <span id="freeText3250415897102429626" style="display:none">This review can also be found at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogspot.ca/2017/04/the-girl-who-was-supposed-to-die-by.html">http://fortheloveofbooksreviews.blogs...</a><br /><br /> She wakes up to two men arguing over whether or not to end her life. She doesn't know her name, she doesn't know where she is, and she doesn't know why one of her fingernails has been pried off of her hand. <br /><br />She manages to escape, but her ordeal is far from over. As she investigates herself, who she is, and what is going on, she gets help from an acquaintance who is determined to solve this mystery with her. Only one thing is for certain...danger is around every corner. <br /><br />It's hard to write a synopsis of this book without giving anything away. The complete mystery of what is going on made this book truly a five-star read, and as my second five-star April Henry novel, I know that I'll be reading her books again. <br /><br />The main character's fear was absolutely palpable from start to finish. I love that the author started the story off with the two men discussing whether or not to murder her, this absolutely drew my attention in and it didn't let me go until I turned to the last page. The little touches, like the main character's injured finger (ouch!) really gave the book an eerie vibe and built suspense. <br /><br />The characters themselves, from the main girl, to the boy who helps her figure out what is going on, worked well with the story, and I think that all of their personalities, relationships, and affiliations contributed to the awesome quality of this novel. As I mentioned, it's hard to say much without giving important pieces of the plot away, so trust me when I say that the explanations behind the characters' motives and situations were far from disappointing. <br /><br />There truly isn't much else that I can say, except that if you like mysteries, you should read this book! I can't say much more because I worry that I'll spoil it somehow!<br /><br />I recommend this to those who like mysteries and thrillers where a lot is at stake. If you're into suspenseful young adult books, this one is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3250415897102429626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2747299924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18199570846049288592">Trigger warnings: amnesia, torture, death, violence, death of a parent (in the past), <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[presumed death of a sibling, animal death <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, fire. <br/><br/>When I finished this last night, I gave it 3.5 stars but on reflection I'm bumping it down to 3 purely because the plot went to some bonkers places that I didn't see coming and it was a pretty weird choice for a YA book tbh. <br/><br/>So this girl wakes up with no memories, right? And there are two guys talking about how they're going to kill</span>
  <span id="freeText18199570846049288592" style="display:none">Trigger warnings: amnesia, torture, death, violence, death of a parent (in the past), <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[presumed death of a sibling, animal death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, fire. <br /><br />When I finished this last night, I gave it 3.5 stars but on reflection I'm bumping it down to 3 purely because the plot went to some bonkers places that I didn't see coming and it was a pretty weird choice for a YA book tbh. <br /><br />So this girl wakes up with no memories, right? And there are two guys talking about how they're going to kill her. And she has to escape and work out who she is blah blah blah. But then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when she finds out who she is, you get this whole plot where her parents are virologists who discover a virulent strain of hantavirus and their company wants to turn it into a biological weapon so now they're on the run with their research and she got captured by the bad guys so they could torture her for her parents' whereabouts????? Like.........??????????? Also they tell her that they murdered her 3 year old brother and bring out a body for her to touch (she's got a bag over her head so she can't see it) but really it's a chimpanzee from the research lab and she definitely believes that it's her brother?!?!?! IDEK. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I mean, I liked the first two thirds of the story. I liked the protagonist and I liked Ty, although <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the last minute romance was wildly unnecessary <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. So I liked it. It was a fast paced and action-packed thriller. It just went to a really strange place... </span>

<div id="review_763000739" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/763000739" />
    <a title="Indi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8008554-indi"><img alt="Indi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599611034p2/8008554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/763000739?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Indi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Indi" href="/user/show/8008554-indi">Indi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=favourite-author">favourite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=would-like-to-eventually-reread">would-like-to-eventually-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=personal-rating-4-stars">personal-rating-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=kidnapping-murder-and-mystery">kidnapping-murder-and-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=f-j">f-j</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8008554-indi?shelf=would-like-to-own">would-like-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer763000739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10516244066206233068"><b>
  <i>Act now. Be.</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>My mind shut down. Went blank. Went somewhere I wouldn’t have to remember. Even when they pulled out my fingernails, it wouldn’t come back.</b><br/><br/>	<br/>She doesn’t know <u>who</u> she is. She doesn’t know <u>where</u> she is. And she doesn’t know <u>what</u> has happened to her. All she knows is that two guys want to kill her. So she must run.<br/><br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book, it was interesting and really reached out and grabbed me. I liked the beginning, a girl who has lost her memory and people are out to kill her. </span>
  <span id="freeText10516244066206233068" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Act now. Be.</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>My mind shut down. Went blank. Went somewhere I wouldn’t have to remember. Even when they pulled out my fingernails, it wouldn’t come back.</b><br /><br />	<br />She doesn’t know <u>who</u> she is. She doesn’t know <u>where</u> she is. And she doesn’t know <u>what</u> has happened to her. All she knows is that two guys want to kill her. So she must run.<br /><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book, it was interesting and really reached out and grabbed me. I liked the beginning, a girl who has lost her memory and people are out to kill her. It really grabs your attention. I liked the characterisation the most. While Cady didn’t have quite so much it was still good enough, but the characterisation of Ty and even James was really good! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ty was the cool sweet underdog but even still not everything about him added up. Why would his parents kick him out just because he trashed a car? Sure it’s REALLY bad, but no normal mother would kick their son out of home for that, and us readers don’t know if Ty’s mother is normal or a drug addict or anything really, so that’s hard to judge. And then even so, if his parents really did kick him out of home because of that I find it hard to believe that Ty would do such a thing. From the book we see him as kind, careful, responsible and mature. Would Ty really have trashed a car? Or is he only responsible and mature now because of the trashing of the car? It really needed to be explained that little but more for us to understand.<br /><br />And the whole thing about Z-Biotech seemed a little far-fetched. I think any other better idea could have been made. And at one point in the book it seemed that the author didn’t know how to continue, which leads me to believe that’s where the idea of the virus came from, just a quick decision to keep the story going. <br /><br />Then there’s the little things that ticked me off, a spelling/grammar mistake (HIs instead of His), the fact that nobody mentioned Cady’s changed hair after it was done (like her mother didn’t even comment on it), the relationship between her and Ty and how fast her memories came back. I mean it was just like BAM! There was no “she looked at the phone on the desk. <i>Her</i> phone on <i>her</i> desk. There was no connection between the sudden flow of her memories coming back. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />All in all, and despite all those flaws that I mentioned (if you peeked), the book was really amazing. So suspenseful and engaging. I highly recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10516244066206233068" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_595881308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/595881308" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/595881308?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=new-author-to-me">new-author-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer595881308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1771889878923576063">The Girl who was Supposed to Die starts off as this creepy thriller where you trust no one and question everything. Imagine waking up somewhere you don’t know with two people who you also don’t know discussing whether or not they should kill you. You’d be pretty freaked out, right? Oh, and what about seeing your fingernails not attached to your fingers? *shudders* I was instantly pulled in.<br/><br/>Who was this girl? Who were these people who held her? What information did she have? Why did they want tha</span>
  <span id="freeText1771889878923576063" style="display:none">The Girl who was Supposed to Die starts off as this creepy thriller where you trust no one and question everything. Imagine waking up somewhere you don’t know with two people who you also don’t know discussing whether or not they should kill you. You’d be pretty freaked out, right? Oh, and what about seeing your fingernails not attached to your fingers? *shudders* I was instantly pulled in.<br /><br />Who was this girl? Who were these people who held her? What information did she have? Why did they want that information? And most importantly, why did they want to kill her?<br /><br />The story is revealed to us in a very smart way. Each chapter was fairly short and abrupt, all ending on a cliff hanger that all but guaranteed you would continue on. They reminded me of episodes of a crime drama honestly. It definitely kept up your frantic emotions to rival the MC’s.<br /><br />But despite the good, there was also come bad. The characters themselves were just completely unbelievable to me and about halfway through, the books plot hit ridiculous. The situations our leads found themselves in were overdramatic and unrealistic and the characters were hard to relate to. For example: Ty. Now, I loved Ty, I really did. But he wasn’t real. Yes, there are people who help other people in need…but what Ty did, no teenage boy is going to do. And the parents, especially the mother, were really hard to swallow with how they reacted to the situations. <br /><br />So overall, even though it wasn’t what I wanted it to be, it did have a good writing technique. Kept me wanting to read, to find out what happened, even if I didn’t believe it when I got there. If you’re looking for a quick, fast moving book with a little bit of mystery, then you might enjoy this book as a fun little read. <br /><br />This review can also be seen <a href="http://www.bookjems.com/2013/08/book-review-girl-who-was-supposed-to.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> at my blog. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1771889878923576063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5123231-irene-mchugh?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2311730877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6801757889635072284">I discovered April Henry on the shelves of the middle school library where I work. Her website tagline is “I kill people, but only on paper.” Muh-wah-ha-ha! Immediately, I was doling her books out to students to see if they liked her style. After a few positive reviews came back, I decided to buy a couple of her books on Audible.<br/><br/>The narrator for this particular novel was fairly awful. Instead of sounding like a teenage girl, her intonation came closer to mimicking Siri. She didn’t sound like a m</span>
  <span id="freeText6801757889635072284" style="display:none">I discovered April Henry on the shelves of the middle school library where I work. Her website tagline is “I kill people, but only on paper.” Muh-wah-ha-ha! Immediately, I was doling her books out to students to see if they liked her style. After a few positive reviews came back, I decided to buy a couple of her books on Audible.<br /><br />The narrator for this particular novel was fairly awful. Instead of sounding like a teenage girl, her intonation came closer to mimicking Siri. She didn’t sound like a machine for the entire story, but enough of it that she grated on my nerves. <br /><br />As far as the story goes, this popcorn fast-paced mystery kept me engaged. The short choppy sentences and cliffhanger moments at the end of chapters reminded me of James Patterson, except for kids. In 213 pages, there are 41 chapters.<br /><br />The opening scene sustains a suspense through the entire first chapter. This teenage girl wakes up not knowing who she is, and she hears men in the next room discussing how to kill her. As she’s dragged out of a cabin and through the woods, she’s problem-solving how she’s going to get away from her captors. And this girl has some Ninja moves!<br /><br />Is she really a teenager?<br />Is she a spy? Like a female Jason Bourne?<br /><br />The action continues to move along at a quick pace. This thriller is enhanced by the short two-day timeline of the story, and the suspicious bio-research company tied to a few of the characters. Also enjoyable is the super subtle romance sub-plot. From Ty’s first meeting with Cady, the girl, it’s obvious he likes her, but there’s no time for ridiculous moments gazing into each other’s eyes when you’re on the run for your life!<br /><br />Are there aspects of this plot that I found implausible? Yep.<br /><br />Did I care? Not one bit. <br /><br />Whee! This five and a half hour read was fun!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6801757889635072284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8196774269801856980"> The book I ready was "The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die," by April Henry. This book is action packed and I would most definitely recommend this book to others. This book is best suited for an audience around the ages of 13 and above. The book begins with the main character, so called Katie inn the beginning, in a cabin in the middle of the woods. She has been kidnapped and she is in pain. Katie doesn't remember who she is or what happened to her. All she knows is that she is on a hard floor, som</span>
  <span id="freeText8196774269801856980" style="display:none"> The book I ready was "The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die," by April Henry. This book is action packed and I would most definitely recommend this book to others. This book is best suited for an audience around the ages of 13 and above. The book begins with the main character, so called Katie inn the beginning, in a cabin in the middle of the woods. She has been kidnapped and she is in pain. Katie doesn't remember who she is or what happened to her. All she knows is that she is on a hard floor, some of her fingernails have been ripped out, and that twos men are talking near her. Katie eventually escapes but she has know idea where she is going. She has a naturally instinct to drive and decided to trust her instinct to get her to safety. Along the way, she meets a boy named Ty and he helps her figure out who she is and hide from the people who want to kill her. My review for this book is one word. Amazing. The book had me lured in after reading the first two pages. While reading this book, you feel so many different ways for the characters. It feels like you are part of the story helping Katie. I am giving this book a rating of five stars because there was no dull moments in this book. Each chapter leaves you on the edge of your seat. Does Katie ever figure out who she really is? Will she finally escape the men who want her dead once and for all? You will have to read the book "The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die," by April Henry.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2917899753" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer423641203746402297">Crime thriller--very popular in my middle school library. I started reading this with an ESL student who asked me to read a book with her to improve her reading and English. We read for 30 minutes a day, 3 days a week, sharing the read-aloud 50/50. We would get so passionate with our opinions, predictions and speculation. I think we both really looked forward to reading time! Unfortunately, it took forever due to state testing and end-of-year field trips interfering with the schedule, and at the</span>
  <span id="freeText423641203746402297" style="display:none">Crime thriller--very popular in my middle school library. I started reading this with an ESL student who asked me to read a book with her to improve her reading and English. We read for 30 minutes a day, 3 days a week, sharing the read-aloud 50/50. We would get so passionate with our opinions, predictions and speculation. I think we both really looked forward to reading time! Unfortunately, it took forever due to state testing and end-of-year field trips interfering with the schedule, and at the end of the year, she had almost 1/3 of the book left to read on her own over the summer. She did take it with her. I just finished with a public library copy, and it was a pretty exciting plot, but I fear that the end was way too complicated for her with her limited English. I look forward to hearing if she was able to stick with it and to comprehend it. If not, we will probably resume in the Fall when she's in 8th grade. <br /><br />All of Henry's books fly off the shelves in my library. I think with the two under my belt, I need not read the rest but know exactly how to sell her work and to whom to recommend the titles: 7th-9th grade students who love crime drama and want a fast-paced plot. Henry ends each chapter with a cliff-hanger; exciting stuff! <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText16965572064167220461" style="display:none">I'm trying to be more tough with my high ratings. Only giving 5 stars to books that just blow me away.<br /><br />I was not expecting this book to be what it was. I honestly expected it to be just another typical YA book but oh fricken boy was I wrong. <br /><br />Not many books keep me up past my bedtime, my sleep is important. I think this was the second? Maybe third book to ever do that. <br /><br />I gave myself some time to think of what I would change in this book, and I can't think of a single thing. I'm happily giving this book the rating it deserves. I'm so pleasantly surprised at how great this book is! So full of twists and turns you'll have no idea what's about to happen! I can't wait to read more from her. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1728858326692357051">This book was truly a great book I would recommend it for sure. This book can get intense so don't read it if you aren't comfortable with that. It leaves you in suspense about the full truth right up until the end, when it all comes together piece by piece. It is about a girl who has lost her memory due to a tragic thing in her life. She doesn't remember anything from before she woke up on a hard floor. As she struggles to regain her memory everything unravels.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1904472832805810223" style="display:none"> The Girl Who Was Supposed to Die by April Henry is now one of my favorite books. I love everything from the begging to the end. The story is about a girl who wakes up unconscious and doesn't remember ANYTHING. She doesn't know who she is, who her family is, or anything. My favorite part of the whole book would have to be when she has to look like boy so the people who are following her won't recognize her. The part I sort of struggled to understand is when she steps into her house with her so called aunt and they figure out who she is. I would 100% recommend this book to anyone who likes suspense and sort of mystery! </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C4PPu3RT2biPrHrUtQRO5ANtSOnZ9qg6CUbr/oiKCLxXA+I2Bt78ECbtnZl8IYXRfyluM1Mu5QUY/+HSV4SXGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g+DhjT5PUzmnla526lyOjoCbdueu0aQG7ORitwXmqAHfYMwATMJ2kQ7USTsjeUW7/N9QPSQJ6Tn9XWib2ug3pA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9202598359834028793">I write mysteries and thrillers. I live in Portland, Oregon with my family.<br/><br/>If you've read one of my books, I would love to hear from you. Hearing from readers makes me eager to keep writing.<br/><br/>When I was 12, I sent a short story about a six-foot tall frog who loved peanut butter to Roald Dahl, the author of Charlie and the Chocolate Factory. He liked it so much he arranged to have it published in an </span>
  <span id="freeText9202598359834028793" style="display:none">I write mysteries and thrillers. I live in Portland, Oregon with my family.<br /><br />If you've read one of my books, I would love to hear from you. Hearing from readers makes me eager to keep writing.<br /><br />When I was 12, I sent a short story about a six-foot tall frog who loved peanut butter to Roald Dahl, the author of Charlie and the Chocolate Factory. He liked it so much he arranged to have it published in an international children's magazine.<br /><br />My dream of writing went dormant until I was in my 30s, working at a corporate job, and started writing books on the side. Those first few years are now thankfully a blur. Now I'm very lucky to make a living doing what I love. I have written 25 novels for adults and teens, with more on the way. My books have gotten starred reviews, been picked for Booksense, translated into six languages, been named to state reading lists, and won the Oregon Book Award. <br /></span>
